I have gone through phases of not listening to zep for months, and then breaking out their catalog and rediscovering why I love them so much.<br /><br />To me Zep had an air of mystery about them, while they could slay you with riff after game changing riff, most of which have shaped modern rock as we know it, but they could also take an acoustic song and make you feel as if you'd been betrayed by the sheer power of it.<br /><br />They touched on many different styles and never tried to play beyond their station, but always tried to do what they did best. They were always trying to be creative as they could and seemed to get better at it over time. While most groups are struggling to stay creative and even together for that matter after 3 albums and tons of tour dates, they were working on what would become a monumental song, and ultimately a legendary album, Stairway to Heaven. While it has been well over played over the year's, one can't deny the shear accomplishment involved in it's power, sound, and relatively even today, as most groups can't craft songs nearly half as good after years of trying as well as having 6 producers and song writers help them do it.<br /><br />Crafting songs is an art form that overly technical players often lose in perfection, jimmy page understood this and that made his leadership of the band instrumental in achieving what they did. A room of four excellent musicians does not make a great band.<br /><br />While some may say that this performance is not their best, I couldn't say, as I was only 4 when they broke up, but it is my favorite, but that may be because it's the one I've listened to most. Many casual fans do not always like when a groups songs do not sound exactly like the album versions. The main problem is the movie is about 1/2 hour too long. The novelty starts to wear off and the movie gets tedious. I am sure this was high tech for 1936.<br />Again, FLASH GORDON is not a typical super hero film. It looks cheap and dated but if you can overlook those facts, you can have some fun.

B0089IGUP4|4.0|Although on their fourth studio album, The Gaslight Anthem, comprised of Alex Levine, Benny Horowitz, Alex Rosamilia and frontman Brian Fallon, release their debut effort on major label Mercury Records. 2010's [[ASIN:B003FK8V7G American Slang]], released on Side One Dummy, was critically acclaimed across the board. 2012's [[ASIN:B0089IGUP4 Handwritten]], which recently gave The Gaslight Album their first top five album (Billboard 200, #3 with 40,000 copies sold), is definitely a consistent and enjoyable follow-up.<br /><br />\\"45,\\" the first single, opens up the effort energetically.  Loud it may be, \\"45\\" never sounds overwrought or overproduced.  Fallon's lead vocals sit atop the production with ease, delivering a nuanced, commanding vocal.  The songwriting is solid and the play on \\"45\\" (as in an old school record), is a brilliant, lyrical touch.<br /><br />\\"Handwritten,\\" the title track is solid as well, opening with neutral vocal syllabic treatment (\\"Wo oh-oh,\\" etc.). The drum groove is superb, highlighted even more by the timbre of the drums within the production. The chordal guitar is biting, contributing greatly to the rock sound.  Perhaps less satisfying than \\"45,\\" \\"Handwritten\\" is nonetheless above average for sure.<br /><br />\\"Here Comes My Man\\" continues the consistency, featuring acoustic guitar to give off a more folksy-rock sound (welcome Bruce Springsteen comparisons now).  The drums are gargantuan, propelling the straight-quarter note feel of the verse.  The song structure is simple, but excellent, highlighted by the lyrics of the chorus: \\"And all my life I never had a chance/don't you think I knew about all your pretty girlfriends/but I waited for you, gave you time to decide/but you never saw it from anybody else's side.\\"<br /><br />\\"Mulholland Drive\\" is a show stopper, initiated by a cool electric guitar riff.  Driven by a four-on-the-floor beat and nuanced, pointed vocals by Fallon, \\"Mulholland Drive\\" is easily the track to beat at this point.  Other highlights include bluesy-sounding guitar on the instrument break - nice `shedding' for sure.<br /><br />\\"Keepsake\\" is another `keepsake' for sure, incorporating a fine easygoing, lazy groove.  A variety of sounds/sound effects characterize this cut, including organ and synthetic effects.  Another well penned refrain sells well: \\"And now nobody move this sweeper/is where I put you down to lay so I can live with it/and in my heart, heart, heart, there are these waters/where I put you down to lay, whiled I learned to live with it.\\" The Gaslight Anthem are on `autopilot.'<br /><br />\\"Too Much Blood\\" confirms the last sentiment, beating out the superb \\"Mulholland Drive\\" for the album's best cut.  A gargantuan sound initiates the cut, assisted further by gritty opening ad libs by Fallon.  The bass and guitar sound incredibly aggressive here, yielding exceptional riffs throughout.  Incorporating another sound guitar solo as well as another solidly penned chorus, \\"Too Much Blood\\" just may be on repeat `too' many times.<br />\\"Howl\\" contrast the mid-tempo grind of \\"Too Much Blood\\" in favor of lightening-speed punk, though with much better intonation as far as vocals are concerned. At only 2:05, the brevity is a selling point.  Basic and simple, the verse/chorus/verse/chorus map works splendidly without `knocking any socks off.'<br /><br />\\"Biloxi Parish\\" joins the elite of Handwritten (\\"45,\\" \\"Mulholland Drive,\\" \\"Too Much Blood\\" and perhaps \\"Keepsake\\") as one of the best cuts.  The tempo is slower, the groove more grinding, and the guitar timbre adjectively is describe as `bluesy.' Fallon's vocals sit atop the production splendidly making \\"Biloxi\\" a cut with few improprieties.<br /><br />\\"Desire\\" contrasts \\"Biloxi\\" with a quicker tempo, which is predictable.  \\"Desire\\" is not bad, though the formula is `tried and true.' Not too shabby.<br /><br />\\"Mae\\" is a stronger cut, again resurrecting a four-on-the-floor groove and truly confirming Bruce Springsteen comparisons.  Vocally, Fallon sounds exceptional, particularly on the chorus: \\"I wanna see you tonight/would you come for a drive/you can lean into me/if you ain't been in love for a while...\\"<br /><br />Closing cut \\"National Anthem\\" is comparable to Springsteen's \\"Devils & Dust,\\" at least in the sound The Gaslight Anthem is aiming for. Opening with acoustic guitar with no percussion and eventually evolving (inclusion of strings), \\"National Anthem\\" is appropriately placed and another victory for the band.<br /><br />Overall, [[ASIN:B0089IGUP4 Handwritten]] is a fine rock album.  In an age where rock doesn't always characterize the forefront of a pop-driven industry, it is nice to hear an effort the likes of Handwritten.  The Gaslight Anthem join the Boss for best rock albums of 2012 easily.ly, Fallon sounds exceptional, particularly on the chorus: \\"I wanna see you tonight/would you come for a drive/you can lean into me/if you ain't been in love for a while...\\"<br /><br />Closing cut \\"National Anthem\\" is comparable to Springsteen's \\"Devils & Dust,\\" at least in the sound The Gaslight Anthem is aiming for. (And boy, I wanted to.)<br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Thomas awakens one day to find himself in a strange elevator, which takes him to a place called the Glade, a large open field surrounded by stone walls. The Glade is populated only by other young people, and none of them remember their lives before they arrived at the Glade the same way Thomas did, one boy each month. As disorienting as his situation is, Thomas tries to figure out exactly what is going on in the Glade, and finds that it is surrounded by a giant stone maze. Each night the walls in the maze move, and there is a group of people, the runners, who explore the maze each day to try and find an escape route. But it's not as easy as it sounds--at night the maze is patrolled by a strange race of deadly creatures called Grievers. One day, a girl unexpectedly arrives in the Glade. And the message she brings with her completely rocks the community the boys have worked to create and causes them to question exactly what they are living for.<br /><br />This is a tremendously creative, intriguing and affecting book. A little bit Lord of the Flies with some of the dystopian elements of the Hunger Games series thrown in, the story is a little confusing to grasp at the start (much as it is for Thomas) but as it unfolds you find yourself wondering what will happen next, and many of the details will surprise you. Some of the characters are a little two-dimensional, but I found myself totally immersed in their situation. I'm so glad that the YA genre has become just as enjoyable and gripping for adults.

9889979942|3.0|Based on the thumbnail image of the book's cover, even with the hot woman and the tasteful design, and knowing only it was some kind of photographic spread on China, I feared \\"coffee table book\\" - or worse, cheesy Chinese variety that would actually mar my coffee table, the sort you can find in the tourist bookshops with washed-out reproductions, incoherent English and sappy token displays of ethnic minorities dancing in their costumes.<br /><br />The actual book, once in my hands, is unlike any other book I've seen, including those in the photojournalism genre. It has a surprisingly small trim size of only 6 x 6 inches, but at 638 pages and over 2 inches thick and weighing almost 3 pounds, it's not a small book (and probably better suited to hardcover than its fragile paper binding). The weight is legitimated on the inside with the high-quality paper stock and what I'd guess approaches 1,000 high-resolution photo reproductions, capturing the author's two years of traveling to every province of China frequently under spartan and the roughest of conditions. Each province is prefaced with a map and a concisely written pitch, along with beautifully succinct, haiku-like captions for many of the photos, demonstrating that the author's skills as a photographer are matched by appropriate writing talent. The descriptions and the variety of photographic subjects - rural and urban landscapes, ordinary daily objects transfigured by the camera, and lots and lots of unforgettable people - seem to form a narrative that pulls one along the lengthy book, though most readers will probably prefer to dip into it at random than go through the whole thing at one shot. Regardless, it fulfills its evident purpose in being a comprehensive and enticing introduction to the country for people who haven't been to China, and equally interesting as well for those conversant with the country (I myself have lived in China for 13 years).<br /><br />Now for a more critical angle. The gold standard of \\"intrepid\\" or \\"hardcore\\" photojournalism books and one that will probably never be equaled is surely [[ASIN:8798170201 American Pictures: A Personal Journey Through the American Underclass]] by the Dane Jacob Holdt. Holdt arrived in the US in 1971 with $40 in his pocket and spent the next 5 years hitchhiking over 100,000 miles through 48 states and living with 350 families, taking 15,000 photos (selling his blood to buy film) and culling them down to 700 in his book, which are balanced by a substantial and moving narrative of his encounters with the many people he met, delving into their lives with a shocking empathy and intimacy (often sleeping with both women and men to dialogue at the deepest human level), and unflinchingly capturing with his lens the most horrific but sympathetic images of poverty and decrepitude.<br /><br />Personally, I would like to see the Chinese equivalent of Holdt's book. I suspect Tom Carter may even have witnessed some such darker scenarios or ruder encounters with people and made an understandable strategic decision not to include them, inasmuch as he seems to be positioning his book at the more \\"polite\\" end of the photojournalism spectrum, calibrated not to ruffle any feathers in China, where only the positive side of things tends to be presented. Thus he does not refer to himself in the first person but adopts the \\"objective\\" reportorial \\"the author,\\" and when he almost dies during extreme weather on the 5,600-meter Drolma-La pass if it weren't for \\"a Ngari pilgrim woman\\" who \\"appeared as my own private Tibetan goddess of mercy, literally carrying me the remainder of the spiritual circuit,\\" that's all we're told. I want more; I want to hear the dark side of travel and see the underbelly of the country, not just the picture-perfect promotional product. The author is certainly qualified to do this, and I invite him to consider these possibilities for another project.
